Father's Intercourse with Son's Slave-Girl: Hanafi Ruling
Ruling on a man who has intercourse with his son's slave-girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a man has intercourse with his son's slave-girl and claims the child, and explain why no dower (mahr) is due.

Core Idea
Father's guardianship creates ownership before intercourse – no mahr, only value.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a nuanced case involving a father's relationship with his son's slave-girl. The Hanafi school rules that if a man has intercourse with his son's slave-girl, she bears a child, and he claims it, he must pay the value of both the slave-girl and the child, but no dower ('aqr) is required. The legal reasoning hinges on the father's guardianship over his son's property, which establishes ownership prior to the intercourse. Let's explore the ruling, its evidence, and the opposing view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and legal consequence
Recognize the scenario: a man has intercourse with his son's slave-girl, she gives birth, and he claims the child. The Hanafi ruling: lineage is established, she becomes umm walad, and he must pay her value and the child's value.
This is the core ruling stated at the beginning of the passage.
2
Determine the hukm level
The payment of value is wajib (obligatory), but no mahr is due. Understand the type of obligation: it's not a penalty but a compensation for ownership transfer.
The text explicitly says 'عليه قيمتها لا عقرها' – he owes her value, not her dower.
3
Analyze the reasoning (talil)
The commentator explains that the father has guardianship (wilayah) over his son's property for necessity. This guardianship allows him to own the slave-girl to preserve his lineage (by claiming the child). Ownership is established before intercourse, so the intercourse is on his own property, eliminating any dower.
The key point: ownership is a condition (shart) for the intercourse to be lawful in terms of avoiding 'aqr.
4
Examine the opposing view
Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) and al-Shafi'i argue that ownership is only established by a legal ruling (hukman), not automatically. Therefore, the intercourse occurred on someone else's property, requiring a mahr.
This is a classic usul difference about the nature of ownership (haqiqatan vs. hukman).
5
Consider practical implications
The dispute has financial consequences: under the Hanafi ruling, the father pays value (which may be less than mahr) and the son receives compensation; under Shafi'i, a full mahr is due. The Hanafi position is the mufta bihi.
This illustrates how a difference in legal reasoning directly affects outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ومن وطى أمة ابنه فولدت فادعاه ثبت نسبه وصارت أم ولده وعليه قيمتها لا عقرها وقيمة ولدها لأن له ولاية تملك مال ابنه للحاجة إلى البقاء فله تملك جارية ابنه للحاجة إلى صيانة الماء. وحاصل وجوه مسألة جارية الابن إذا ولدت من الأب فادعاه ست وتسعون لأنه إما أن يصدقه الابن أو يكذبه أو يدعيه معه أو يسكت، وكل من الأربعة إما أن تكون قنة أو مدبرة أوأم ولد أو مكاتبة وكل من الستة عشر إما أن تكون كلها له أو بينه وبين أجنبي أو بينه وبين أبيه وكل من الثمانية والأربعين إما أن يكون الأب أهلاً للولاية أو لا غير أن الحاجة إلى إبقاء نسله دونها إلى إبقاء نفسه فلهذا يمتلك الجارية بالقيمة والطعام بغير القيمة، ثم هذا الملك يثبت قبيل الاستيلاد شرطاً له إذا المصحح حقيقة الملك أو حقه وكل ذلك غير ثابت للأب فيها حتى يجوز له التزوج بها فلا بد من تقديمه، فتبين أن الوطء يلاقي ملكه فلا يلزمه العقر وقيمة الولد . وقال زفر والشافعي يلزمه المهر لأنهما يثبتان الملك حكما
His saying: (And whoever has intercourse with his son's slave-girl, and she gives birth, and he claims the child, his lineage is established, she becomes umm walad, and he owes her value, not the dower for intercourse, and the value of her child). Because he has guardianship over his son's property due to the need for survival, so he can own his son's slave-girl due to the need to protect his lineage. The total aspects of the issue of the son's slave-girl, if she gives birth from the father and he claims it, are ninety-six: because either the son confirms him, denies him, claims it together with him, or remains silent. Each of these four: either she is a qinn, mudabbirah, umm walad, or mukatabah. Each of these sixteen: either she is entirely his, or shared with a stranger, or shared with his father. Each of these forty-eight: either the father is qualified for guardianship or not. However, the need to preserve his lineage is less than the need to preserve his own life, so he owns the slave-girl by paying value, just as he owns food without value. Then this ownership is established right before the conception as a precondition for him, because what validates is actual ownership or a right, and none of that is established for the father regarding her such that he could marry her, so it must be prior. Thus it becomes clear that the intercourse meets his ownership, so he does not owe the 'aqr (dower for intercourse) nor the value of the child. Zufar and al-Shafi'i said that he owes the mahr because they consider ownership as established by legal ruling.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with a specific case: a man has intercourse with his son's slave-girl, she becomes pregnant and gives birth, and the man (the grandfather) claims the child as his. The ruling: the child's lineage is established to the father, the slave-girl becomes umm walad (mother of the child, thus free upon the father's death), and he must pay her current value and the child's value. He does not owe 'aqr (a type of mahr for doubtful intercourse) because he owns the slave-girl by virtue of his guardianship over his son's property to preserve his own lineage. The commentator explains that this ownership is established right before the intercourse, so the intercourse is on his own property. Zufar and al-Shafi'i disagree, saying he owes the mahr because ownership is only established by the court's ruling, not automatically. The text also outlines the many possible variations (96) based on the son's response and the status of the slave-girl.

Key Terms
أم ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who bears a child to her master, thus becoming free upon his death.
العقر (al-'aqr): A compensation for intercourse under doubtful circumstances; akin to mahr.
الولاية (al-wilayah): Guardianship; here the father's authority over his son's property for necessities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man has intercourse with his son's slave-girl and she gives birth to a child he claims, what does the Hanafi school require him to pay?
A) Only the child's value
B) The slave-girl's value and the child's value
C) The mahr ( 'aqr) and the child's value
D) Nothing at all

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a father who has intercourse with his son's slave-girl and claims the child incurs no dower because his guardianship establishes prior ownership, requiring only payment of her value and the child's value.
